Question:
How would you define a colloid and how does it compare to a suspension in terms of particle size?

Options:
a. Colloids consist of larger particles than suspensions.
b. Suspensions have smaller particle sizes than colloids.
c. Colloids have particle sizes between those of solutions and suspensions.
d. There is no difference in particle size between colloids and suspensions.


Correct Answer: গ

Solution:
সমাধান:
1. কোলোইডের সংজ্ঞা: কোলোইড হলো সেই মিশ্রণ যেখানে কণার আকার সাধারণত [math]1\ \text{nm}–1000\ \text{nm}[/math] সীমার মধ্যে থাকে, ফলে এগুলো ম্যাক্সস্কোপিকভাবে দেখা যায় না কিন্তু টিন্ডাল প্রভাব সৃষ্টি করতে পারে।  
2. তুলনা: দ্রবণে কণার আকার খুবই ছোট (প্রায় [math]1000\ \text{nm}[/math])। তাই কোলোইডের কণার আকার দ্রবণ ও সাসপেনশনের মাঝামাঝি থাকে।  
3. ফলাফল: উপরোক্ত কারণে গ (c) সঠিক।  
অন্যান্য বিকল্পগুলির খণ্ডন: (a) ভুল—কোলোইডে সাসপেনশনের তুলনায় ছোট কণা থাকে; (b) ভুল—সাসপেনশনে কণা বড় হয়; (d) ভুল—তিনটির মধ্যে কণার আকারে সুস্পষ্ট পার্থক্য আছে।

Question #573 (ID: 24127)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: MCQ | Book: বিজ্ঞান | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
What is the effect of increasing temperature on the solubility of sugar in water compared to table salt?

Options:
a. Both sugar and salt have increased solubility.
b. Sugar's solubility increases, while salt's solubility decreases.
c. Salt's solubility increases, while sugar's solubility decreases.
d. Sugar's and salt's solubility is unaffected by temperature.


Correct Answer: ক

Solution:
Solution:
Step 1: General rule — for most solid solutes in water the solubility increases with temperature because dissolution is often endothermic; raising temperature shifts the equilibrium to favor more dissolved solute (Le Chatelier’s principle).  
Step 2: Sugar (sucrose) is markedly more soluble in hot water than in cold, so its solubility increases with temperature.  
Step 3: Common table salt (sodium chloride) shows a small but positive increase in solubility as temperature rises (it does not decrease appreciably).  
Conclusion: Therefore both sugar and salt have increased solubility with increasing temperature, so option a is correct. Options b and c are incorrect because salt does not decrease while sugar increases (b), nor does sugar decrease while salt increases (c); option d is incorrect because solubility is affected by temperature.

Explanation:

Question #574 (ID: 24128)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: MCQ | Book: বিজ্ঞান | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Which method would be most effective to separate a solid from a liquid in a suspension?

Options:
a. Evaporation
b. Filtration
c. Distillation
d. Decantation


Correct Answer: খ

Solution:
Solution:
Step 1: Recognize that a suspension contains insoluble solid particles dispersed in a liquid; the solid particles are large enough to be physically separated.  
Step 2: Use filtration — place filter paper in a funnel and pour the suspension through it. The solid particles are retained on the filter paper while the liquid (filtrate) passes through, giving a clear separation.  
Step 3: Conclude that option (b) Filtration is most effective because it physically traps insoluble solids. Evaporation removes the liquid slowly and may leave residues or change substances, distillation separates based on boiling points (unnecessary for insoluble solids), and decantation is less complete because some solid remains in the poured liquid.

Explanation:

Question #575 (ID: 24129)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: MCQ | Book: বিজ্ঞান | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
What is the primary reason that some mixtures are classified as homogeneous while others are classified as heterogeneous?

Options:
a. Homogeneous mixtures have uniform composition, whereas heterogeneous mixtures do not.
b. Heterogeneous mixtures consist of only solids, while homogeneous mixtures consist of liquids.
c. Homogeneous mixtures are always solutions, while heterogeneous mixtures are always suspensions.
d. There is no distinction; all mixtures are the same.


Correct Answer: ক

Solution:
Solution:
Step 1: Define the terms — a homogeneous mixture has the same composition and appearance throughout (no visible separate parts), while a heterogeneous mixture has non-uniform composition with distinct phases or visible components.  
Step 2: Compare options — a states the uniform vs non-uniform distinction, which matches the standard definitions, so it is correct.  
Step 3: Explain why others are wrong — b is incorrect because heterogeneous mixtures can be liquids or gases as well as solids; c is incorrect because not all homogeneous mixtures are only solutions (examples include alloys) and heterogeneous mixtures are not always suspensions (they can be colloids or mixtures with visible phases); d is false because a clear distinction exists.  

Answer: a

Explanation:
